The game will feature vibrant and colorful visuals, reminiscent of the original Mario Sunshine game, but with a new twist of encountering ink monsters and navigating through ink-infested landscapes. The addition of co-op gameplay and the ability to upgrade flood's powers will addmore depth and variety to the gameplay. The ink monsters will pose different challenges, requiring players to strategically use flood's upgraded nozzles to defeat them. The open-world design of Isle Delfino and the other islands will encourage exploration and discovery, with hidden secrets and collectibles scattered throughout the game.  As players progress through the game and collect Shine Sprites, they will unlock new areas and uncover the truth behind Bowser's plans. The story will also feature comedic moments and interactions with memorable characters, adding to the overall charm and fun of the game.  Additionally, the game will introduce new mechanics and gameplay elements, such as platforming challenges where players must navigate through treacherous ink platforms and races against time to complete missions. These new elements will keep the gameplay fresh and exciting, appealing to both new and longtime fans of the Mario franchise.  Overall, Mario Sunshine 2: Ink Invasion will provide players with a captivating and immersive gaming experience, combining the beloved elements of the original Mario Sunshine game with new challenges, powers, and a compelling storyline. It will be a worthy successor to the original, bringing joy and excitement to players of all ages.

First time I've been as excited for a 2D Mario game as for a 3D Mario game.  Also, anyone who claims SMB Wonder looks like a mobile game has exactly ZERO idea about stylization. Any visual artwork can use strong stylization, that just means it doesn't look like anything else on the market. Ever seen the Spider-Verse movies?  Many mobile games, especially adaptations of console or PC games, use strong stylization to mask the lack of detail due to the weak graphics processors of cell phones. SMB Wonder, on the other hand, makes a deliberate decision to use a surrealistic style and has tremendous detail work in every animation, e.g. the facial expressions, smearframes, model deformations, etc. The comic book-like special effects are just as intentional.  Anyone who doesn't like this style seems to want the vanilla standard graphics of the NSMB games back, after complaining that 2D Mario games never try anything new.

Okay, now THIS is more like it! The first look we got of this game didn't impress me much. The 2D series has become old and stale. It's always the same thing, we get new power-ups, a few new enemies and such, but that's pretty much it. The series was in desperate need of something new added to the gameplay to take the series to the next level, much the way SMB3 did with the world map, flight, and item inventory, and the way SMW did with Yoshi, an upgraded and improved world map, and secret exits. The "New" series didn't really add anything new beyond multiplayer co-op. But now, we FINALLY get the next big step up for the series with badges, a very unique and innovative online multiplayer, and an open world map! This is a pretty huge deal! wait this is THE best mario game so far dude
Great looking game! They added a ton of new features over NSMBUD, which makes it worth it to try day 1. The Wonder feature brings back "random" chaos and definitely can be fun in a friend/family session where winning isn't always the main goal. Also new is that Bowser merged with the castle (like Marik w/ Ra in Yu-Gi-Oh).  The new badges help players with cool abilities, but I wonder if those are just enhancements to already existing abilities. I liked the vine shooting (ala Spiderman) and the ability to travel just underground. Even the Safety Badge is useful for difficult courses or inexperienced players going over lava. I do like the ghost feature and the standee feature. Being able to revive others makes it more fun for everyone.  There also did not appear to be any time countdown, which is a blessing. The game has so much happening that having the stress of a time limit won't make the experience fun, so I'm glad they took it away (please confirm if this is correct). I also like wandering around the map to complete different stages in any order (within reason). It makes for an open world type experience so the game doesn't have be played linearly all the time.  For the co-op mode, local co-op looks fine. As long as players don't bounce off each other and accidentally kill each other like in NSMBUD I'm all for it. For the online co-op, we can see other players there, but what happens when you are ready to move on? I guess no matter what part of the stage you are in, whatever online players there are at that part of the stage will also be there. Pretty nifty as there could be several online players playing the same stage but at different parts of it.  What I did not like was the statement "they all play the same", when the announcer referred to the human characters. Did they take away the uniqueness of Peach, Luigi, Daisy, and Mario and simply move those traits into the badges? I surely hope not because I want to be able to float with Peach's dress, or jump a bit higher when I'm Luigi.  Overall, the game looks solid and based on this trailer, I would rate it a 8.5/10. That red OLED Switch looks nice, but it's not an improvement if I'm playing on TV with my original Switch. Will definitely get the game upon release as it's been a good while since their last 2D side scrolling adventure.

I'm super happy that a lot of Super Mario World elements are found in this game, considering I have always wanted a modern sequel to the former game: - The world map really reminds me of the layout of SMW (especially W1). Even some of the level designs and backgrounds also got quite heavily inspired. - Bowser using the Wonder Flower and transformed into a gigantic floating castle actually looks like an evolution of SMW final castle with his floating clownface car lurking in the dark sky - Characters floating using their hats, looks like how they descend with a cape feather, and Mario's animations are recreations of his old posture in SMW. - P-Balloon transformation from the Wonder Flower - SMW sound effects (burrowing into the ground = destroying rotating blocks), riding on Yoshi (I guess it's an evolution) - The pipe designs look like in SMW - Upward shell or item throwing (this was seriously needed long ago)  At the same time, this also really makes some big steps away from the "New Super" series, and I love that they are somehow going back to their original roots with SMB3 and especially SMW influences.  10/10 ğŸ’•
